I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
path filtering on merge commits silently skips changes
Other recent work intersected with the issue originally reported in #3475. With ample hindsight, the issue being reported by #3475 was legitimate -- apologies to both @nghazali and @dooman87. I think we all got hung up on debating a wrong solution and it clouded our view of what the actual problem was. There was a lot of discussion of the `-m` flag, which actually would have tipped things too far in the opposite direction, resulting in many false positive commit selections.

Let's give this another try.

## The problem

When `NewestFromBranch` walks a branch's history with `includePaths` configured, for each commit, it finds files the commit touched by running:

```
git show --pretty= --name-only <commitID>
```

For a regular commit, this shows files changed relative to that commit's one parent. For a merge commit, this commit produces a combined diff, which only lists files that differ from *all* parents. For a clean merge with no conflicts, this produces empty output (every file in the result matches at least one parent, so nothing appears in the combined diff).

The result: clean merge commits are invisible to path filtering. The history walk moves on to that commit's parents. Either or both of those may match the path filter, but may be missing content brought into the branch by the other parent.

## Demonstration (no Kargo involved)

```sh
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
export GIT_PAGER=cat

# Setup
dir=$(mktemp -d)
echo "Working in $dir"
cd "$dir"
git init -b main
mkdir -p {foo,bar}

echo "base" > foo/file1.txt
echo "base" > foo/file2.txt
echo "base" > bar/other.txt
git add . && git commit -m "initial"

# Branch A: touches foo/file1.txt
git checkout -b branch-a
echo "changed by branch-a" > foo/file1.txt
git add . && git commit -m "branch-a: modify file1"

# Branch B: touches foo/file2.txt
git checkout main
git checkout -b branch-b
echo "changed by branch-b" > foo/file2.txt
git add . && git commit -m "branch-b: modify file2"

# Merge B then A into main
git checkout main
git merge branch-b --no-ff -m "merge branch-b"
git merge branch-a --no-ff -m "merge branch-a"
MERGE_A=$(git rev-parse HEAD)

echo ""
echo "=== git log ==="
git log --oneline --graph

echo ""
echo "=== git show on merge commit: no flags (current behavior) ==="
git show --pretty= --name-only "$MERGE_A"
echo "(empty — combined diff, merge commit invisible to path filtering)"

# Cleanup hint
echo ""
echo "Cleanup: rm -rf $dir"
```

Sample output:

```
=== git log ===
*   e5fdb29 merge branch-a
|\
| * 1a510c7 branch-a: modify file1
* |   78884a9 merge branch-b
|\ \
| |/
|/|
| * afa608f branch-b: modify file2
|/
* 25c01af initial

=== git show on merge commit: no flags (current behavior) ===
(empty — combined diff, merge commit invisible to path filtering)
```

The merge commit is essentially invisible, exactly as #3475 said.

Here's what we extensively debated in #3475, tacked on toward the end of the script:

```sh
echo ""
echo "=== git show on merge commit: -m ==="
git show --pretty= --name-only -m "$MERGE_A"
echo "(shows files from both parent diffs — noisy, includes false positives)"
```

Sample output:

```
=== git show on merge commit: -m ===
foo/file1.txt
foo/file2.txt
(shows files from both parent diffs — noisy, includes false positives)
```

This is no good. The changes to `foo/file2.txt` were not actually introduced by this merge commit (e5fdb29). They were already on the branch, having already been introduced by a different merge commit (78884a9).

Proposing a different solution:

```sh
echo "=== git show on merge commit: --first-parent ==="
git show --pretty= --name-only --first-parent "$MERGE_A"
echo "(shows only what the merge introduced to main — correct)"
```

```
=== git show on merge commit: --first-parent ===
foo/file1.txt
(shows only what the merge introduced to main — correct)
```

This correctly identifies `foo/file1.txt` as the only change introduced to main by the merge commit (e5fdb29).

</pr_description>

    34	type newestFromBranchSelector struct {
    35	        *baseSelector

    37

    50	func newNewestFromBranchSelector(
    51	        sub kargoapi.GitSubscription,
    52	        creds *git.RepoCredentials,
    53	) (Selector, error) {
    54	        base, err := newBaseSelector(sub, creds)
    55	        if err != nil {
    56	                return nil, fmt.Errorf("error building base selector: %w", err)
    57	        }
    58	        s := &newestFromBranchSelector{
    59	                baseSelector: base,
    60	                branch:       sub.Branch,
    61	        }
    62	        s.selectCommitsFn = s.selectCommits
    63	        s.listCommitsFn = s.listCommits
    64	        s.getDiffPathsForCommitIDFn = s.getDiffPathsForCommitID
    65	        return s, nil
    66	}

    68	// MatchesRef implements Selector.
    69	func (n *newestFromBranchSelector) MatchesRef(ref string) bool {
    70	        if !strings.HasPrefix(ref, branchPrefix) {
    71	                return false // Doesn't look like a branch ref
    72	        }
    73	        branch := strings.TrimPrefix(ref, "refs/heads/")
    74	        if n.branch == "" {
    75	                // Note: We do not require branch to be specified in the subscription.
    76	                // When it is not specified, the subscription is implicitly for the
    77	                // repository's default branch. We don't really know what the repository's
    78	                // default branch is, so we make two imperfect assumptions here:
    79	                //   1. The default branch is either "main" or "master".
    80	                //   2. The repository does not have BOTH a main and master branch.
    81	                return branch == "main" || branch == "master"
    82	        }
    83	        return n.branch == branch
    84	}
    85	
    86	// Select implements the Selector interface.
    87	func (n *newestFromBranchSelector) Select(ctx context.Context) (
    88	        []kargoapi.DiscoveredCommit,
    89	        error,
    90	) {
    91	        loggerCtx := append(
    92	                n.getLoggerContext(),
    93	                "selectionStrategy", kargoapi.CommitSelectionStrategyNewestFromBranch,
    94	                "branch", n.branch,
    95	        )
    96	        logger := logging.LoggerFromContext(ctx).WithValues(loggerCtx...)
    97	        ctx = logging.ContextWithLogger(ctx, logger)
    98	
    99	        logger.Debug("cloning repository")
   100	        repo, err := n.gitCloneFn(
   101	                n.repoURL,
   102	                &git.ClientOptions{
   103	                        Credentials:           n.creds,
   104	                        InsecureSkipTLSVerify: n.insecureSkipTLSVerify,
   105	                },
   106	                &git.CloneOptions{
   107	                        Branch:       n.branch,
   108	                        SingleBranch: true,
   109	                        Filter:       git.FilterBlobless,
   110	                },
   111	        )
   112	        if err != nil {
   113	                return nil, fmt.Errorf("error cloning git repo %q: %w", n.repoURL, err)
   114	        }
   115	        defer func() {
   116	                _ = repo.Close()
   117	        }()
   118	
   119	        commits, err := n.selectCommitsFn(repo)
   120	        if err != nil {
   121	                return nil,
   122	                        fmt.Errorf("error selecting relevant commits from branch: %w", err)
   123	        }
   124	
   125	        return n.commitsToAPICommits(ctx, commits), nil
   126	}
   127	
   128	func (n *newestFromBranchSelector) selectCommits(
   129	        repo git.Repo,
   130	) ([]git.CommitMetadata, error) {
   131	        selectedCommits := make([]git.CommitMetadata, 0, n.discoveryLimit)
   132	        for skip, batch := uint(0), uint(n.discoveryLimit); ; skip, batch = skip+batch, min(batch*2, 1000) { // nolint: gosec
   133	                commits, err := n.listCommitsFn(repo, batch, skip) // nolint: gosec
   134	                if err != nil {
   135	                        return nil,
   136	                                fmt.Errorf("error listing commits from git repo %q: %w", n.repoURL, err)
   137	                }
   138	
   139	                if len(commits) == 0 {
   140	                        break
   141	                }
   142	
   143	                // If no filters are specified, return the first commits up to the limit.
   144	                if n.includePaths == nil && n.excludePaths == nil && n.filterExpression == nil {
   145	                        return trimSlice(commits, n.discoveryLimit), nil
   146	                }
   147	
   148	                for _, commit := range commits {
   149	                        // Filter commits based on expressions.
   150	                        include, err := n.evaluateCommitExpression(commit)
   151	                        if err != nil {
   152	                                return nil, fmt.Errorf("error evaluating filter expression: %w", err)
   153	                        }
   154	                        if !include {
   155	                                continue
   156	                        }
   157	
   158	                        // If include or exclude path selectors are specified, filter the commits.
   159	                        if n.includePaths != nil || n.excludePaths != nil {
   160	                                diffPaths, err := n.getDiffPathsForCommitIDFn(repo, commit.ID)
   161	                                if err != nil {
   162	                                        return nil, fmt.Errorf(
   163	                                                "error getting diff paths for commit %q in git repo %q: %w",
   164	                                                commit.ID,
   165	                                                n.repoURL,
   166	                                                err,
   167	                                        )
   168	                                }
   169	                                if !n.MatchesPaths(diffPaths) {
   170	                                        continue
   171	                                }
   172	                        }
   173	
   174	                        // If we reach this point, the commit got past all the filters.
   175	                        selectedCommits = append(selectedCommits, commit)
   176	
   177	                        if len(selectedCommits) >= n.discoveryLimit {
   178	                                return trimSlice(selectedCommits, n.discoveryLimit), nil
   179	                        }
   180	                }
   181	        }
   182	
   183	        return trimSlice(selectedCommits, n.discoveryLimit), nil
   184	}
   185	
   186	func (n *newestFromBranchSelector) listCommits(
   187	        repo git.Repo,
   188	        limit uint,
   189	        skip uint,
   190	) ([]git.CommitMetadata, error) {
   191	        return repo.ListCommits(limit, skip) // nolint: gosec
   192	}
   193	
   194	func (n *newestFromBranchSelector) getDiffPathsForCommitID(
   195	        repo git.Repo,
   196	        commitID string,
   197	) ([]string, error) {
   198	        return repo.GetDiffPathsForCommitID(commitID)
   199	}
   200	
   201	// evaluateCommitExpression evaluates the given commit expression against
   202	// the given commit metadata. The commit metadata is passed as the environment
   203	// for the expression evaluation. It returns true if the expression evaluates to
   204	// true, and false otherwise. If the expression is not a boolean, it is
   205	// converted to a boolean using strconv.ParseBool. If the conversion fails,
   206	// an error is returned.
   207	func (n *newestFromBranchSelector) evaluateCommitExpression(
   208	        commit git.CommitMetadata,
   209	) (bool, error) {
   210	        if n.filterExpression == nil {
   211	                return true, nil
   212	        }
   213	
   214	        env := map[string]any{
   215	                "id":         commit.ID,
   216	                "commitDate": commit.CommitDate,
   217	                "author":     commit.Author,
   218	                "committer":  commit.Committer,
   219	                "subject":    commit.Subject,
   220	        }
   221	
   222	        result, err := expr.Run(n.filterExpression, env)
   223	        if err != nil {
   224	                return false, err
   225	        }
   226	
   227	        switch result := result.(type) {
   228	        case bool:
   229	                return result, nil
   230	        default:
   231	                parsedBool, err := strconv.ParseBool(fmt.Sprintf("%v", result))
   232	                if err != nil {
   233	                        return false, err
   234	                }
   235	                return parsedBool, nil
   236	        }
   237	}
   238	
   239	func (n *newestFromBranchSelector) commitsToAPICommits(
   240	        ctx context.Context,
   241	        commits []git.CommitMetadata,
   242	) []kargoapi.DiscoveredCommit {
   243	        logger := logging.LoggerFromContext(ctx)
   244	        apiCommits := make([]kargoapi.DiscoveredCommit, 0, len(commits))
   245	        for _, meta := range commits {
   246	                apiCommits = append(apiCommits, kargoapi.DiscoveredCommit{
   247	                        ID:     meta.ID,
   248	                        Branch: n.branch,
   249	                        // A decent subject length for a commit message is 50 characters
   250	                        // (based on the 50/72 rule). We are nice people, and allow a
   251	                        // bit more. But not an excessive amount, to minimize the risk of
   252	                        // exceeding the maximum size of the object in the API server.
   253	                        Subject:     shortenString(meta.Subject, 80),
   254	                        Author:      meta.Author,
   255	                        Committer:   meta.Committer,
   256	                        CreatorDate: &metav1.Time{Time: meta.CommitDate},
   257	                })
   258	                logger.Trace(
   259	                        "discovered commit from branch",
   260	                        "commit", meta.ID,
   261	                        "creatorDate", meta.CommitDate.Format(time.RFC3339),
   262	                )
   263	        }
   264	        logger.Debug("discovered commits", "count", len(commits))
   265	        return apiCommits
   266	}

   418	func (w *workTree) GetDiffPathsForCommitID(commitID string) ([]string, error) {
   419	        resBytes, err := libExec.Exec(w.buildGitCommand("show", "--pretty=", "--name-only", commitID))
   420	        if err != nil {
   421	                return nil, fmt.Errorf("error getting diff paths for commit %q: %w", commitID, err)
   422	        }
   423	        var paths []string
   424	        scanner := bufio.NewScanner(bytes.NewReader(resBytes))
   425	        scanner.Split(bufio.ScanLines)
   426	        for scanner.Scan() {
   427	                paths = append(
   428	                        paths,
   429	                        scanner.Text(),
   430	                )
   431	        }
   432	        return paths, nil
   433	}

Now I can see the issue clearly. Line 419:

```
git show --pretty= --name-only <commitID>
```

This command, when run on a merge commit, produces a combined diff which only lists files that differ from *all* parents. For a clean merge, this produces empty output.

The PR description says the fix should use `--first-parent` flag:

```
git show --pretty= --name-only --first-parent <commitID>
```

This would show only what the merge introduced to the main branch, which is the correct behavior.

    71	func Test_parseTagMetadataLine(t *testing.T) {
    72	        tests := []struct {
    73	                name    string
    74	                line    string
    75	                want    TagMetadata
    76	                wantErr bool
    77	        }{
    78	                {
    79	                        name:    "incorrect number of fields",
    80	                        line:    "tag3|*|commitid3|*|subject3|*|author3",
    81	                        wantErr: true,
    82	                },
    83	                {
    84	                        name: "lightweight tag",
    85	                        line: "tag1|*|commitid1|*|subject1|*|author1|*|committer1|*|2024-01-01 12:00:00 -0500",
    86	                        want: TagMetadata{
    87	                                Tag:         "tag1",
    88	                                CommitID:    "commitid1",
    89	                                Subject:     "subject1",
    90	                                Author:      "author1",
    91	                                Committer:   "committer1",
    92	                                CreatorDate: mustParseTime("2024-01-01 12:00:00 -0500"),
    93	                        },
    94	                },
    95	                {
    96	                        name: "annotated tag with extra |*| in annotation",
    97	                        line: "tag2|*|commitid2|*|subject2|*|author2|*|committer2|*|" +
    98	                                "2024-01-01 12:00:00 -0500|*|tagger2|*|annotation with |*| inside",
    99	                        want: TagMetadata{
   100	                                Tag:         "tag2",
   101	                                CommitID:    "commitid2",
   102	                                Subject:     "subject2",
   103	                                Author:      "author2",
   104	                                Committer:   "committer2",
   105	                                CreatorDate: mustParseTime("2024-01-01 12:00:00 -0500"),
   106	                                Tagger:      "tagger2",
   107	                                Annotation:  "annotation with |*| inside",
   108	                        },
   109	                },
   110	        }
   111	
   112	        for _, tt := range tests {
   113	                t.Run(tt.name, func(t *testing.T) {
   114	                        got, err := parseTagMetadataLine([]byte(tt.line))
   115	                        if tt.wantErr {
   116	                                require.Error(t, err)
   117	                        } else {
   118	                                require.NoError(t, err)
   119	                                require.Equal(t, tt.want, got)
   120	                        }
   121	                })
   122	        }
   123	}

cd /tmp && cat > reproduce.sh << 'EOF'
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
export GIT_PAGER=cat

# Setup
dir=$(mktemp -d)
echo "Working in $dir"
cd "$dir"
git init -b main 2>/dev/null || git init && git checkout -b main
mkdir -p {foo,bar}

echo "base" > foo/file1.txt
echo "base" > foo/file2.txt
echo "base" > bar/other.txt
git add . && git commit -m "initial"

# Branch A: touches foo/file1.txt
git checkout -b branch-a
echo "changed by branch-a" > foo/file1.txt
git add . && git commit -m "branch-a: modify file1"

# Branch B: touches foo/file2.txt
git checkout main
git checkout -b branch-b
echo "changed by branch-b" > foo/file2.txt
git add . && git commit -m "branch-b: modify file2"

# Merge B then A into main
git checkout main
git merge branch-b --no-ff -m "merge branch-b"
git merge branch-a --no-ff -m "merge branch-a"
MERGE_A=$(git rev-parse HEAD)

echo ""
echo "=== git log ==="
git log --oneline --graph

echo ""
echo "=== git show on merge commit: no flags (current behavior) ==="
git show --pretty= --name-only "$MERGE_A"
echo "(empty — combined diff, merge commit invisible to path filtering)"

echo ""
echo "=== git show on merge commit: -m ==="
git show --pretty= --name-only -m "$MERGE_A"
echo "(shows files from both parent diffs — noisy, includes false positives)"

echo ""
echo "=== git show on merge commit: --first-parent ==="
git show --pretty= --name-only --first-parent "$MERGE_A"
echo "(shows only what the merge introduced to main — correct)"

# Cleanup
rm -rf "$dir"
EOF

#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
export GIT_PAGER=cat

# Setup
dir=$(mktemp -d)
echo "Working in $dir"
cd "$dir"
git init -b main
git config user.email "test@test.com"
git config user.name "Test"
mkdir -p foo bar

echo "base" > foo/file1.txt
echo "base" > foo/file2.txt
echo "base" > bar/other.txt
git add . && git commit -m "initial"

# Branch A: touches foo/file1.txt
git checkout -b branch-a
echo "changed by branch-a" > foo/file1.txt
git add . && git commit -m "branch-a: modify file1"

# Branch B: touches foo/file2.txt
git checkout main
git checkout -b branch-b
echo "changed by branch-b" > foo/file2.txt
git add . && git commit -m "branch-b: modify file2"

# Merge B then A into main
git checkout main
git merge branch-b --no-ff -m "merge branch-b"
git merge branch-a --no-ff -m "merge branch-a"
MERGE_A=$(git rev-parse HEAD)

echo ""
echo "=== git log ==="
git log --oneline --graph

echo ""
echo "=== git show on merge commit: no flags (current behavior) ==="
git show --pretty= --name-only "$MERGE_A"
echo "(empty — combined diff, merge commit invisible to path filtering)"

echo ""
echo "=== git show on merge commit: -m ==="
git show --pretty= --name-only -m "$MERGE_A"
echo "(shows files from both parent diffs — noisy, includes false positives)"

echo ""
echo "=== git show on merge commit: --first-parent ==="
git show --pretty= --name-only --first-parent "$MERGE_A"
echo "(shows only what the merge introduced to main — correct)"

rm -rf "$dir"
EOF
bash reproduce.sh

Good - the mock just delegates to the function, so no changes needed there.

Now let me think about edge cases:

1. **Regular (non-merge) commits**: `--first-parent` on a regular commit behaves the same as without it - the commit has only one parent, so `--first-parent` doesn't change anything. ✅

2. **Merge commits**: With `--first-parent`, it shows the diff of the merge commit against its first parent (the branch being merged into). This is exactly what we want - it shows what was introduced by the merge. ✅

3. **Tag-based selectors**: Tags can point to any commit (regular or merge). If a tag points to a merge commit, using `--first-parent` is also the correct behavior - it shows what that merge introduced to its first-parent line. ✅

4. **Commit with no parents (root commit)**: `git show --first-parent` on a root commit should work fine - it shows all files in the initial commit. ✅

The fix is minimal and correct. Let me now also verify the fix works end-to-end with a script that simulates what the code does:







🎬 ACTION
cd /tmp && cat > test_fix.sh << 'EOF'
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail

dir=$(mktemp -d)
echo "Working in $dir"
cd "$dir"
git init -b main
git config user.email "test@test.com"
git config user.name "Test"
mkdir -p foo bar

echo "base" > foo/file1.txt
echo "base" > foo/file2.txt
echo "base" > bar/other.txt
git add . && git commit -m "initial"

# Branch A: touches foo/file1.txt
git checkout -b branch-a
echo "changed by branch-a" > foo/file1.txt
git add . && git commit -m "branch-a: modify file1"

# Branch B: touches foo/file2.txt
git checkout main
git checkout -b branch-b
echo "changed by branch-b" > foo/file2.txt
git add . && git commit -m "branch-b: modify file2"

# Merge B then A into main
git checkout main
git merge branch-b --no-ff -m "merge branch-b"
MERGE_B=$(git rev-parse HEAD)
git merge branch-a --no-ff -m "merge branch-a"
MERGE_A=$(git rev-parse HEAD)

echo ""
echo "=== Testing with --first-parent (new behavior) ==="

echo ""
echo "--- Merge A (should show only file1.txt):"
git show --pretty= --name-only --first-parent "$MERGE_A"

echo ""
echo "--- Merge B (should show only file2.txt):"
git show --pretty= --name-only --first-parent "$MERGE_B"

echo ""
echo "--- Regular commit (should show its changes normally):"
git show --pretty= --name-only --first-parent $(git rev-parse branch-a)

echo ""
echo "--- Root commit (should show all files):"
git show --pretty= --name-only --first-parent $(git rev-list --max-parents=0 HEAD)

echo ""
echo "All checks passed!"

rm -rf "$dir"
EOF
bash test_fix.sh

+        //
+        // They are designed to output the following fields, separated by `|*|`:
+        // - tag name
+        // - commit ID
+        // - subject
+        // - author name and email
+        // - committer name and email
+        // - creator date
+        //
+        // For annotated tags, we also output the following fields:
+        // - tagger name and email
+        // - tag annotation (the first line of the tag message)
+        //
+        // The `if`/`then`/`else` logic is used to ensure that we get the commit ID
+        // and subject of the tag, regardless of whether it's an annotated or
+        // lightweight tag.
+        //
+        // nolint: lll
+        const (
+                formatAnnotatedTag   = `%(refname:short)|*|%(*objectname)|*|%(*contents:subject)|*|%(*authorname) %(*authoremail)|*|%(*committername) %(*committeremail)|*|%(creatordate:iso8601)|*|%(taggername) %(taggeremail)|*|%(contents:subject)`
+                formatLightweightTag = `%(refname:short)|*|%(objectname)|*|%(contents:subject)|*|%(authorname) %(authoremail)|*|%(committername) %(committeremail)|*|%(creatordate:iso8601)`
+                tagFormat            = `%(if)%(*objectname)%(then)` + formatAnnotatedTag + `%(else)` + formatLightweightTag + `%(end)`
+        )
+
+        tagsBytes, err := libExec.Exec(w.buildGitCommand(
+                "for-each-ref",
+                "--sort=-creatordate",
+                "--format="+tagFormat,
+                "refs/tags",
+        ))
+        if err != nil {
+                return nil, fmt.Errorf(
+                        "error listing tags for repo %q: %w",
+                        w.originalURL, err,
+                )
+        }
+
+        var tags []TagMetadata
+        scanner := bufio.NewScanner(bytes.NewReader(tagsBytes))
+        for scanner.Scan() {
+                tag, err := parseTagMetadataLine(scanner.Bytes())
+                if err != nil {
+                        return nil, err
+                }
+                tags = append(tags, tag)
+        }
+
+        return tags, nil
 }

+                        return fmt.Errorf("sparse checkout pattern must be relative: %s", p)
+                }

+                        return fmt.Errorf("sparse checkout pattern cannot escape repository: %s", p)
+                }
+                // Cone mode only supports directory patterns, not globs
+                if strings.ContainsAny(p, "*?[") {

+                                "sparse checkout pattern cannot contain glob characters (*, ?, [): %s; "+
+                                        "use directory paths like 'src/app' instead",
+                                p,
+                        )
+                }
+        }

+                return nil, fmt.Errorf("error configuring the credentials: %w", err)
+        }
+        br, err := LoadBareRepo(repoPath, &LoadBareRepoOptions{
+                Credentials: opts.Credentials,
+        })
+        if err != nil {
+                return nil, err
+        }
+        w.bareRepo = br.(*bareRepo) // nolint: forcetypeassert
+        return w, nil
 }

+                // This author + committer is specific to this commit, so we will override

+                // configuring the user information "globally" within it, and then ensuring
+                // the git commit command uses that home directory.

+                                        Error(cleanErr, "error removing virtual home directory", "path", homeDir)

+                        return fmt.Errorf(

+        if opts.AllowEmpty {
+                cmdTokens = append(cmdTokens, "--allow-empty")
+        }
+
+        cmd := w.buildGitCommand(cmdTokens...)
+        if homeDir != "" {
+                // Override the home directory set by b.buildGitCommand().
+                w.setCmdHome(cmd, homeDir)
+        }
+        if _, err := libExec.Exec(cmd); err != nil {
+                return fmt.Errorf("error committing changes: %w", err)
+        }
+        return nil

+        if _, err := libExec.Exec(w.buildGitCommand("fetch", "origin", "--tags")); err != nil {
+                return nil, fmt.Errorf(
+                        "error fetching tags from repo %q: %w",
+                        w.originalURL, err,

+        //
+        // They are designed to output the following fields, separated by `|*|`:
+        // - tag name
+        // - commit ID
+        // - subject
+        // - author name and email
+        // - committer name and email
+        // - creator date
+        //
+        // For annotated tags, we also output the following fields:
+        // - tagger name and email
+        // - tag annotation (the first line of the tag message)
+        //
+        // The `if`/`then`/`else` logic is used to ensure that we get the commit ID
+        // and subject of the tag, regardless of whether it's an annotated or
+        // lightweight tag.
+        //
+        // nolint: lll
+        const (
+                formatAnnotatedTag   = `%(refname:short)|*|%(*objectname)|*|%(*contents:subject)|*|%(*authorname) %(*authoremail)|*|%(*committername) %(*committeremail)|*|%(creatordate:iso8601)|*|%(taggername) %(taggeremail)|*|%(contents:subject)`

+                tagFormat            = `%(if)%(*objectname)%(then)` + formatAnnotatedTag + `%(else)` + formatLightweightTag + `%(end)`
+        )
+
+        tagsBytes, err := libExec.Exec(w.buildGitCommand(
+                "for-each-ref",
+                "--sort=-creatordate",
+                "--format="+tagFormat,
+                "refs/tags",
+        ))

+                return nil, fmt.Errorf(
+                        "error listing tags for repo %q: %w",
+                        w.originalURL, err,
+                )

+

+        scanner := bufio.NewScanner(bytes.NewReader(tagsBytes))
+        for scanner.Scan() {
+                tag, err := parseTagMetadataLine(scanner.Bytes())
+                if err != nil {
+                        return nil, err
+                }
+                tags = append(tags, tag)
+        }
+
+        return tags, nil

+        // it takes precedence and the tag will be pushed -- the branch will not.

func (w *workTree) GetDiffPathsForCommitID(commitID string) ([]string, error) {$
        resBytes, err := libExec.Exec(w.buildGitCommand("show", "--pretty=", "--name-only", "--first-parent", commitID))$
        if err != nil {$
                return nil, fmt.Errorf("error getting diff paths for commit %q: %w", commitID, err)$
        }$
        var paths []string$
        scanner := bufio.NewScanner(bytes.NewReader(resBytes))$
        scanner.Split(bufio.ScanLines)$
        for scanner.Scan() {$
                paths = append($
                        paths,$
                        scanner.Text(),$
                )$
        }$
        return paths, nil$
}$

+				logging.LoggerFromContext(context.TODO()).
+					Error(cleanErr, "error removing virtual home directory", "path", homeDir)
+			}
+		}()
+		if err = w.setupUser(homeDir, opts.Author); err != nil {
+			return fmt.Errorf(
+				"error setting up author + committer information for commit command: %w", err,
+			)
+		}
+	}
+
+	cmdTokens := []string{"commit", "-m", message}
+	if opts.AllowEmpty {
+		cmdTokens = append(cmdTokens, "--allow-empty")
+	}
+
+	cmd := w.buildGitCommand(cmdTokens...)
+	if homeDir != "" {
+		// Override the home directory set by b.buildGitCommand().
+		w.setCmdHome(cmd, homeDir)
+	}
+	if _, err := libExec.Exec(cmd); err != nil {
+		return fmt.Errorf("error committing changes: %w", err)
+	}
+	return nil
 }

+	}

+	return commits, nil

+	if _, err := libExec.Exec(w.buildGitCommand("fetch", "origin", "--tags")); err != nil {
+		return nil, fmt.Errorf(
+			"error fetching tags from repo %q: %w",
+			w.originalURL, err,
+		)
+	}
+
+	// These formats are quite complex, so we break them down into smaller
+	// pieces for readability.
+	//
+	// They are designed to output the following fields, separated by `|*|`:
+	// - tag name
+	// - commit ID
+	// - subject
+	// - author name and email
+	// - committer name and email
+	// - creator date
+	//
+	// For annotated tags, we also output the following fields:
+	// - tagger name and email
+	// - tag annotation (the first line of the tag message)
+	//
+	// The `if`/`then`/`else` logic is used to ensure that we get the commit ID
+	// and subject of the tag, regardless of whether it's an annotated or
+	// lightweight tag.
+	//
+	// nolint: lll
+	const (
+		formatAnnotatedTag   = `%(refname:short)|*|%(*objectname)|*|%(*contents:subject)|*|%(*authorname) %(*authoremail)|*|%(*committername) %(*committeremail)|*|%(creatordate:iso8601)|*|%(taggername) %(taggeremail)|*|%(contents:subject)`
+		formatLightweightTag = `%(refname:short)|*|%(objectname)|*|%(contents:subject)|*|%(authorname) %(authoremail)|*|%(committername) %(committeremail)|*|%(creatordate:iso8601)`
+		tagFormat            = `%(if)%(*objectname)%(then)` + formatAnnotatedTag + `%(else)` + formatLightweightTag + `%(end)`
+	)
+
+	tagsBytes, err := libExec.Exec(w.buildGitCommand(
+		"for-each-ref",
+		"--sort=-creatordate",
+		"--format="+tagFormat,
+		"refs/tags",
+	))
+	if err != nil {
+		return nil, fmt.Errorf(
+			"error listing tags for repo %q: %w",
+			w.originalURL, err,
+		)
+	}
+
+	var tags []TagMetadata
+	scanner := bufio.NewScanner(bytes.NewReader(tagsBytes))
+	for scanner.Scan() {
+		tag, err := parseTagMetadataLine(scanner.Bytes())
+		if err != nil {
+			return nil, err
+		}
+		tags = append(tags, tag)
+	}
+
+	return tags, nil
 }

+        // branch.
+        LastCommitID() (string, error)
+        // ListTags returns a slice of tags in the repository with metadata such as
+        // commit ID, creator date, and subject.
+        ListTags() ([]TagMetadata, error)
+        // ListCommits returns a slice of commits in the current branch with
+        // metadata such as commit ID, commit date, and subject.
+        ListCommits(limit, skip uint) ([]CommitMetadata, error)
+        // CommitMessage returns the text of the most recent commit message associated
+        // with the specified commit ID.
+        CommitMessage(id string) (string, error)
+        // Push pushes from the local repository to the remote repository.
+        Push(*PushOptions) error
+        // RefsHaveDiffs returns whether there is a diff between two commits/branches
+        RefsHaveDiffs(commit1 string, commit2 string) (bool, error)
+        // RemoteBranchExists returns a bool indicating if the specified branch exists
+        // in the remote repository.
+        RemoteBranchExists(branch string) (bool, error)
+        // ResetHard performs a hard reset on the working tree.
+        ResetHard() error
+        // URL returns the remote URL of the repository.
+        URL() string
+        // UpdateSubmodules updates the submodules in the working tree.
+        UpdateSubmodules() error
 }

+                // This author + committer is specific to this commit, so we will override
+                // repository-level user information by creating a temporary home directory,
+                // configuring the user information "globally" within it, and then ensuring
+                // the git commit command uses that home directory.

+                                logging.LoggerFromContext(context.TODO()).
+                                        Error(cleanErr, "error removing virtual home directory", "path", homeDir)
+                        }

+                        return fmt.Errorf(
+                                "error setting up author + committer information for commit command: %w", err,

+

+        if opts.AllowEmpty {
+                cmdTokens = append(cmdTokens, "--allow-empty")
+        }
+
+        cmd := w.buildGitCommand(cmdTokens...)
+        if homeDir != "" {
+                // Override the home directory set by b.buildGitCommand().
+                w.setCmdHome(cmd, homeDir)
+        }
+        if _, err := libExec.Exec(cmd); err != nil {
+                return fmt.Errorf("error committing changes: %w", err)
+        }
+        return nil

+        scanner := bufio.NewScanner(bytes.NewReader(tagsBytes))
+        for scanner.Scan() {
+                tag, err := parseTagMetadataLine(scanner.Bytes())
+                if err != nil {
+                        return nil, err
+                }
+                tags = append(tags, tag)
+        }
+
+        return tags, nil

+        }

+        // Initialize sparse checkout in cone mode (fast, directory-based)
+        if _, err := libExec.Exec(
+                w.buildGitCommand("sparse-checkout", "init", "--cone"),
+        ); err != nil {
+                return fmt.Errorf("error initializing sparse checkout: %w", err)
+        }
+
+        // Set the sparse checkout patterns
+        setArgs := append([]string{"sparse-checkout", "set"}, patterns...)
+        if _, err := libExec.Exec(w.buildGitCommand(setArgs...)); err != nil {
+                return fmt.Errorf("error setting sparse checkout patterns %v: %w", patterns, err)
+        }
+        return nil
 }
